## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a reactant concentration in a chemical reaction. The rate law dA/dt typically depends on the concentration A raised to the reaction order, and time t may appear if there are external driving forces or if the system has been reduced from a multi-species model.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated first-order kinetics)
- Inhibited reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Parallel pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (multiple reaction channels with baseline)
- Damköhler-type with time: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (concentration and time-dependent rate)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate with reverse reactions)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration power-law dependence (dA/dt ~ A^n) indicates a simple elementary reaction of order n
- A constant offset term in the rate law suggests a reversible reaction approaching equilibrium or a source/production term
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(K+A)) indicate saturation or enzyme-mediated mechanisms where binding sites become limiting
- Product terms like A*(c-A) suggest autocatalytic behavior where the product catalyzes the reaction and total mass is conserved
- If the rate depends explicitly on time t (not just through A), this suggests external forcing, photochemical initiation, or catalyst deactivation
- Negative leading coefficient in the rate law indicates consumption/decay of the reactant, positive indicates production
- A squared denominator term (1+A^2) suggests substrate inhibition where excess reactant slows the reaction
- Half-integer or fractional powers of A (e.g., A^0.5) often arise from chain reaction mechanisms involving radical intermediates
- Exponential dependence on time (exp(c*t)) in the rate may indicate temperature ramping via Arrhenius coupling or catalyst poisoning
- Multiple additive terms with different powers of A suggest competing parallel reaction mechanisms

Set c4=0, combine c0+c3. **MATCH**

**Candidate 9:** `A*c0 + A*c1*log(c2*t+1) + A*c3/(A²+c4)`
